<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> – Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Margot_Wallstr%C3%B6m" title="Margot Wallström">Margot Wallström</a> described it as "a decision to leave humanity's last chance of securing our children's future on this planet".<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> – President <a href="/wiki/Doris_Leuthard" title="Doris Leuthard">Doris Leuthard</a> said the decision was "regrettable".<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> – The Presidential Office efforts to continue the Paris agreement despite Trump's climate decision.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> – The Vice President said Tanzania will continue supporting the agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> – Mehmet Emin Birpınar, Turkey's chief climate negotiator, expressed hope that other countries will not follow Trump, and affirmed Turkey's commitment despite the agreement's "unfairness".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/46px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> – Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Enele_Sopoaga" title="Enele Sopoaga">Enele Sopoaga</a> said that the US had "abandoned" them.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_Uganda.svg/23px-Flag_of_Uganda.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_Uganda.svg/35px-Flag_of_Uganda.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_Uganda.svg/45px-Flag_of_Uganda.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> – Nicholas Ssenyonjo said "the US is the biggest contributor to pollution globally. Pulling out of the Paris agreement means that they do not care about the effects of their pollution to third world countries like Uganda."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> – Marashi, the chairperson of the Emirates Environmental Group (EEG), said that Trump's decision is "unfortunate".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="341" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> – A spokesman for U.N. Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> described Trump's decision as "a major disappointment".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> – Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> expressed her disappointment during a telephone call with Trump, and reaffirmed the United Kingdom's commitment to the agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> She said on live TV, "I have spoken to Donald Trump and told him that the UK believes in the Paris agreement"<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Scotland%27s_First_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland&#39;s First Minister">Scotland's First Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Sturgeon" title="Nicola Sturgeon">Nicola Sturgeon</a> saw it as an "appalling abdication of leadership" that May's signature was lacking from a joint declaration by the leaders of Germany, France and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/23px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/35px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/45px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> – The Minister for Housing, Land Planning &amp; Environment pointed out the deep disappointment about the withdrawal in a joint statement.<sup id="cite_ref-twitter.com_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/16px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/24px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" />&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a> – Bishop <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_S%C3%A1nchez_Sorondo" title="Marcelo Sánchez Sorondo">Marcelo Sánchez Sorondo</a>, Chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Pontifical Academy of Sciences">Pontifical Academy of Sciences</a>, described the withdrawal as a "huge slap in the face" to the world.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> – The Zambian minister for Water Development, Sanitation and Environmental Protection, Lloyd Kaziya, described the withdrawal as "a serious tragedy" to developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/46px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="420" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> – Zhakata said Zimbabwe remained committed to the treaty, but the US withdrawal will make it more difficult for the country.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_industry">Business and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Business and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Coalition_for_Clean_Coal_Electricity" title="American Coalition for Clean Coal Electricity">American Coalition for Clean Coal Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Energy" title="Peabody Energy">Peabody Energy</a>, the largest listed coal producer in the United States, applauded the decision, claiming the result will be lower energy prices and greater reliability of supply.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the day of Trump's predicted withdrawal, 25 companies placed a full-page open letter to President Trump in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>, encouraging the administration to keep the U.S. in the Paris Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The companies were:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blue_Cross_Blue_Shield_of_Massachusetts" title="Blue Cross Blue Shield of Massachusetts">Blue Cross Blue Shield</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Danfoss" title="Danfoss">Danfoss</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dignity_Health" title="Dignity Health">Dignity Health</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gap_Inc." title="Gap Inc.">Gap</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Hartford" title="The Hartford">The Hartford</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard_Enterprise" title="Hewlett Packard Enterprise">Hewlett Packard Enterprise</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ingersoll_Rand" title="Ingersoll Rand">Ingersoll Rand</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls" title="Johnson Controls">Johnson Controls</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Levi_Strauss_%26_Co." title="Levi Strauss &amp; Co.">Levi Strauss &amp; Co.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mars_Incorporated" class="mw-redirect" title="Mars Incorporated">Mars</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Grid_plc" title="National Grid plc">National Grid</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pacific_Gas_and_Electric_Company" title="Pacific Gas and Electric Company">PG&amp;E</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DSM_(company)" title="DSM (company)">Royal DSM</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salesforce.com" title="Salesforce.com">Salesforce.com</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schneider_Electric" title="Schneider Electric">Schneider Electric</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany &amp; Co.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VF_Corporation" title="VF Corporation">VF</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Following Trump's announcement, <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> reaffirmed their support for the Paris Agreement and for measures to tackle climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a> pledged $15&#160;million to the UN Framework Convention on Climate Change Executive Secretariat, explaining: "Americans will honor and fulfill the Paris Agreement by leading from the bottom up – and there isn't anything Washington can do to stop us".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Shortly following Trump's announcement, thirty city mayors, three state governors, more than eighty university presidents and the leaders of more than a hundred businesses joined Bloomberg in opening negotiations with the United Nations to submit a plan for limiting American climate-change emissions in accord with the Paris Agreement guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Blankfein" title="Lloyd Blankfein">Lloyd Blankfein</a> described Trump's decision as "a setback for the environment and for the U.S.'s leadership position in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Immelt" title="Jeff Immelt">Jeff Immelt</a> stated that "climate change is real".<sup id="cite_ref-greenwood1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenwood1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Multiple tech company executives—including Google CEO <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a>, Microsoft President and Chief Legal Officer Brad Smith, Apple CEO <a href="/wiki/Tim_Cook" title="Tim Cook">Tim Cook</a>, Facebook CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> CEO Jeff Immelt—condemned the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a> said Microsoft believes that "climate change is an urgent issue that demands global action." Google's <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a> tweeted "Disappointed with today's decision. Google will keep working hard for a cleaner, more prosperous future for all". Facebook's <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a> said "Withdrawing from the Paris climate agreement is bad for the environment, bad for the economy, and it puts our children's future at risk."
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Resignations_from_presidential_advisory_boards_in_protest">Resignations from presidential advisory boards in protest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Resignations from presidential advisory boards in protest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Two business leaders resigned from Trump advisory boards in protest to his decision to withdraw. <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla, Inc.</a> and <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a>, resigned from the two presidential advisory councils on which he had sat. Musk stated: "Climate change is real. Leaving Paris is not good for America or the world."<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Iger" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Iger">Robert Iger</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>, also resigned, saying "As a matter of principle, I've resigned from the President's Council over the Paris Agreement withdrawal."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._public_opinion">U.S. public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: U.S. public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Paris Agreement is broadly popular among Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> A national poll by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Council_on_Global_Affairs" title="Chicago Council on Global Affairs">Chicago Council on Global Affairs</a> conducted in June 2016  found that 71 percent of American adults favored U.S. participation in the Paris Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Similar, a November 2016 poll conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Yale_Program_on_Climate_Change_Communication" title="Yale Program on Climate Change Communication">Yale Program on Climate Change Communication</a> found that 69 percent of U.S. registered voters favored U.S. participation in the Paris Agreement, while just 13 percent were opposed.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Trump's decision to withdraw the U.S. from the accord was seen as an attempt to appeal to his <a href="/wiki/Base_(politics)" title="Base (politics)">base</a>, even at the risk of alienating Democrats and independent voters.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> This strategy diverged from the typical approach taken by most U.S. presidents, who historically have sought to appeal to the center.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_177-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> A <i>New York Times</i> analysis described the move as "a daring and risky strategy" taken by "the first president in the history of polling to govern without the support of a majority of the public from the start of his tenure," adding: "In effect, Mr. Trump is doubling down on presiding as a minority president, betting that when the time comes, his fervent supporters will matter more, especially clustered in key Midwest states."<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_177-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i>/ABC News <a href="/wiki/Public_opinion" title="Public opinion">public opinion</a> survey of American adults, conducted from June 2–4, 2017, found that 59 percent opposed Trump's decision to withdraw the U.S. from the Paris Agreement, and just 28 percent supported it. Asked about the effect of withdrawal on the U.S. economy, 42 percent said it would hurt the economy; 32 percent believed it would help the economy; and 20 percent believed that it would make no difference.<sup id="cite_ref-ClementDavisPoll_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClementDavisPoll-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WashPoPollDetails_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPoPollDetails-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The poll showed a sharp division among partisan lines: 67 percent of Republicans supported Trump's decision, but just 22 percent of <a href="/wiki/Independent_(voter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent (voter)">independents</a> and 8 percent of Democrats supported it.<sup id="cite_ref-ClementDavisPoll_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClementDavisPoll-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic">Domestic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Domestic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, in an editorial, stated that "There was no&#160;greatness in the decision he rendered Thursday, just the heightened&#160;prospect of a&#160;climate-stricken globe left&#160;behind for future generations."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> called it "disgraceful" and stated that Trump "knows nothing or cares little about the science underlying the stark warnings of environmental disruption."<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For their edition of June 2, 2017, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i> revived their famous 1975 "Ford to City: Drop Dead" cover with a photo of Trump and the words "Trump to World: Drop Dead".<sup id="cite_ref-sfgate-1jun2017_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate-1jun2017-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Times" title="Tampa Bay Times">Tampa Bay Times</a></i> criticized the move, writing that it would especially endanger coastal states such as Florida, which are already suffering from <a href="/wiki/Rising_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Rising sea level">rising sea levels</a>, which damage property and infrastructure and harm the drinking water supply.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Detroit_Free_Press" title="Detroit Free Press">Detroit Free Press</a></i> stated that "President Donald Trump has betrayed the future of our children, our grandchildren, and our planet".<sup id="cite_ref-:12_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a> stated that "Under Trump, the U.S. has already become an irresponsible role model."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_San_Diego_Union-Tribune" title="The San Diego Union-Tribune">The San Diego Union-Tribune</a></i> stated that "President Trump is ushering in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Century" title="Chinese Century">Chinese Century</a>" and called it the worst decision of Trump's life.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A piece by commentator <a href="/wiki/Erick_Erickson" title="Erick Erickson">Erick Erickson</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> described the withdrawal from the Paris Agreement as the correct move, for the reason that "climate change is [not] an issue worth caring much about".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_E._Schoen" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas E. Schoen">Douglas E. Schoen</a>, also writing for Fox, contrarily said that a withdrawal from the Paris Agreement "only hastens America's retreat from global political and economic leadership".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign">Foreign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foreign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Foreign coverage of Trump's announcement was overwhelmingly unfavorable.  A lead in the British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> said that the decision would be unlikely to stunt the growth of renewable energy, and suggested that "a much more likely casualty of Trump's choice is the US economy he claims to be protecting".<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The British newspaper <i>The Independent</i> noted the "tension between myth and reality" in Trump's withdrawal speech.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The German tabloid <i><a href="/wiki/Berliner_Kurier" title="Berliner Kurier">Berliner Kurier</a></i> ran a headline "Erde an Trump: Fuck You!" ("Earth to Trump: Fuck You!").<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>China's <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua</a> state news agency called the withdrawal a "global setback."<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i> said that
</p>
<blockquote><p>In the long catalogue of destructive things that Donald Trump has inflicted on the United States and the world, pulling out of the most important global attempt to slow the impact of climate change must go down as the worst.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protests">Protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Protest_(35042111665).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg/220px-Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg/330px-Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg/440px-Paris_Protest_%2835042111665%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Protest_(35042111665).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesters in Washington, D.C., the day of the announcement</div></div></div>
<p>Protesters gathered at the White House gates on the day of the announcement.<sup id="cite_ref-thehill-1jun2017-1_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehill-1jun2017-1-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nye" title="Bill Nye">Bill Nye</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Science_communication" title="Science communication">science communicator</a> and television personality known for making scientific concepts more accessible to the general public, was one of the protesters in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-thehill-1jun2017-2_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehill-1jun2017-2-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/John_A._Wilson_Building" title="John A. Wilson Building">John A. Wilson Building</a> in D.C. was lit in green in protest of the decision,<sup id="cite_ref-nbcwash-1jun2017_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbcwash-1jun2017-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> as were <a href="/wiki/One_World_Trade_Center" title="One World Trade Center">One World Trade Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kosciuszko_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosciuszko Bridge">Kosciuszko Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">New York City Hall</a> in New York City, <a href="/wiki/Boston_City_Hall" title="Boston City Hall">Boston City Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_City_Hall" title="Montreal City Hall">Montreal City Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville,_Paris" title="Hôtel de Ville, Paris">Hôtel de Ville</a> in Paris, and the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_Revoluci%C3%B3n" title="Monumento a la Revolución">Monumento a la Revolución</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angel_of_Independence" title="Angel of Independence">Angel of Independence</a> in Mexico City.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn-1jun2017_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-1jun2017-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo-2jun2017_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-2jun2017-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Protests also occurred in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nbcny-1jun2017_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbcny-1jun2017-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-miami-1jun2017_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miami-1jun2017-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-sd-1jun2017_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sd-1jun2017-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cny-1jun2017_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cny-1jun2017-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
